// To install: pnpm i @tavily/core

const { tavily } = require('@tavily/core');
const client = tavily({ apiKey: "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" });
client.crawl("tavily.com", {
    instructions: "Get all pages on developer document",
    limit: 200,
    maxDepth: 5,
    maxBreadth: 100,
    extractDepth: "advanced",
    format: "text",
    selectDomains: [
        "tavily.com"
        ],
    includeImages: true,
    includeFavicon: true,
    includeUsage: true
})
.then(console.log);

Similar to other search engines, Tavily employs a web crawler to discover new web pages and index their content. Tavily Search and its underlying index are designed to support the legitimate interests of internet users by providing access to web information.       "raw_content": "Traditional search APIs such as Google, Serp and Bing retrieve search results based on a user query. However, the results are sometimes irrelevant to the goal of the search, and return simple URLs and snippets of content which are not always relevant. Because of this, any developer would need to then scrape the sites to extract relevant content, filter irrelevant information, optimize the content to fit LLM context limits, and more. This task is a burden and requires a lot of time and effort to complete. The Tavily Search API takes care of all of this for you in a single API call. The Tavily Search API aggregates up to 20 sites per a single API call, and uses proprietary AI to score, filter and rank the top most relevant sources and content to your task, query or goal. In addition, Tavily [...] Building an AI agent that leverages realtime online information is not a simple task. Scraping doesn’t scale and requires expertise to refine, current search engine APIs don’t provide explicit information to queries but simply potential related articles (which are not always related), and are not very customziable for AI agent needs. This is why we’re excited to introduce the first search engine for AI agents - Tavily. Tavily is a search engine optimized for LLMs, aimed at efficient, quick and persistent search results. Unlike other search APIs such as Serp or Google, Tavily focuses on optimizing search for AI developers and autonomous AI agents. No credit card required.\n​ Pricing Overview\nTavily operates on a simple, credit-based model: [...] ​ Tavily Extract\nThe number of successful URL extractions and your extraction depth determines the cost of your request. You never get charged if a URL extraction fails.\n\nBasic Extract (basic): Every 5 successful URL extractions cost 1 API credit\nAdvanced Extract (advanced): Every 5 successful URL extractions cost 2 API credits\n\n​ Tavily Map\nThe number of pages mapped and whether or not natural-language instructions are specified determines the cost of your request. You never get charged if a map request fails.\n\nRegular Mapping: Every 10 successful pages returned cost 1 API credit\nMap with (instructions): Every 10 successful pages returned cost 2 API credits\n\n​ Tavily Crawl\nTavily Crawl combines both mapping and extraction operations, so the cost is the sum of both: [...] Crawl Cost = Mapping Cost + Extraction Cost\n\nFor example:\n\nIf you crawl 10 pages with basic extraction depth, you’ll be charged 1 credit for mapping (10 pages) + 2 credits for extraction (10 successful extractions ÷ 5) = 3 total credits\nIf you crawl 10 pages with advanced extraction depth, you’ll be charged 1 credit for mapping + 4 credits for extraction = 5 total credits\n\n​ Tavily Research (beta)\nTavily Research follows a dynamic pricing model with minimum and maximum credit consumption boundaries associated with each request. The minimum and maximum boundaries differ based on if the request uses model=mini or model=pro.\n\nRequest Cost Boundaries\nmodel=pro\nmodel=mini\n\nPer-request minimum\n15 credits\n4 credits\n\nPer-request maximum\n250 credits\n110 credits\n\nQuickstartRate Limits",

The Tavily Search crawler does not advertise a differentiated user agent because we must avoid discrimination from websites that allow only Google to crawl them. However, if a domain or page is not crawlable by Googlebot, then Tavily Search’s bot will not crawl it either.\nIndexing and Delisting\n\nrobots.txt is not used to prevent a page from being indexed. Instead, a site owner can delist a page by using the robots noindex directive.\nOnce your web page has been updated with this directive, Tavily needs to re-fetch it to apply the changes.\n\n​ Right to Be Forgotten\nIf your inquiry is about delisting web pages containing personal data about you, please follow the guidance and process of the right to be forgotten.\n​ Reporting Non-Existent Pages\nIn case Tavily Search is returning a page that no longer exists, and you would like to have it delisted, you may contact us at [email protected].\nPrivacy PolicyFrequently Asked Questions",

You never get charged if a URL extraction fails.\n\nBasic Extract (basic): Every 5 successful URL extractions cost 1 API credit\nAdvanced Extract (advanced): Every 5 successful URL extractions cost 2 API credits\n\n​ Tavily Map\nThe number of pages mapped and whether or not natural-language instructions are specified determines the cost of your request.       "raw_content": "Tavily Docs home page\n\nHomeIntroductionAPI & SDKsEcosystemExamplesChangelogHelp\n\n API Playground\n Community\n Blog\n\n##### API Reference\n\n POST\n POST\n POST\n POST\n GET\n\n SDK Reference\n\n##### JavaScript\n\n Quickstart\n SDK Reference\n\n##### Best Practices\n\n Search\n Extract\n Crawl\n Research\n API Key Management\n\nPython SDK\n\nCopy\n\nAsk AI\n\n```\nfrom tavily import TavilyClient from  tavily import  TavilyClient tavily_client = TavilyClient(api_key=\"tvly-YOUR_API_KEY\") tavily_client = TavilyClient(api_key =\"tvly-YOUR_API_KEY\")response = tavily_client.extract(\" response = tavily_client.extract(\" print(response) print(response)\n```\n\nCopy\n\nAsk AI [...] ​\n\nchunks\\_per\\_source\n\ninteger\n\ndefault:3\n\nChunks are short content snippets (maximum 500 characters each) pulled directly from the source. Use `chunks_per_source` to define the maximum number of relevant chunks returned per source and to control the `raw_content` length. Chunks will appear in the `raw_content` field as:  `[...] [...]` . Similar to other search engines, Tavily employs a web crawler to discover new web pages and index their content. The index we build is completely independent of other search engines, and all search results are exclusively served from this index. Tavily Search and its underlying index are designed to support the legitimate interests of internet users by providing access to web information. In cases where indexing involves processing personal data, Tavily—as the controller of the index—relies on legitimate interests as defined under Article 6(1)(f) of the EU “General Data Protection Regulation” (GDPR), as well as other applicable data protection laws. [...] Contact the Website Owner: Request that the site removes your personal data, as it may otherwise be reindexed.\n Update Your Website: If the data appears on your own site, verify that it isn’t hard-coded (for example, in a business address or telephone number). You can check by right-clicking on the page, selecting “View source,” and using Ctrl + F to search for the data. Once updated or removed, you can submit your page to be re-fetched.\n Use Privacy Controls: For data on social media platforms, adjust available privacy settings to keep your data private.\n\nIf you wish to prevent search engines from indexing your page, please follow the instructions provided on this page.\n\n### ​ Submitting an RTBF or right to object request",

      "raw_content": "Traditional search APIs such as Google, Serp and Bing retrieve search results based on a user query. However, the results are sometimes irrelevant to the goal of the search, and return simple URLs and snippets of content which are not always relevant. Because of this, any developer would need to then scrape the sites to extract relevant content, filter irrelevant information, optimize the content to fit LLM context limits, and more. This task is a burden and requires a lot of time and effort to complete. The Tavily Search API takes care of all of this for you in a single API call. The Tavily Search API aggregates up to 20 sites per a single API call, and uses proprietary AI to score, filter and rank the top most relevant sources and content to your task, query or goal. In addition, Tavily [...] Building an AI agent that leverages realtime online information is not a simple task. Scraping doesn’t scale and requires expertise to refine, current search engine APIs don’t provide explicit information to queries but simply potential related articles (which are not always related), and are not very customziable for AI agent needs. This is why we’re excited to introduce the first search engine for AI agents - Tavily. Tavily is a search engine optimized for LLMs, aimed at efficient, quick and persistent search results. Unlike other search APIs such as Serp or Google, Tavily focuses on optimizing search for AI developers and autonomous AI agents. We take care of all the burden of searching, scraping, filtering and extracting the most relevant information from online sources. All in a [...] Quickstart",

No credit card required.\n\n## ​ Pricing Overview\n\nTavily operates on a simple, credit-based model: [...] Regular Mapping: Every 10 successful pages returned cost 1 API credit\n Map with (`instructions`): Every 10 successful pages returned cost 2 API credits\n\n### ​ Tavily Crawl\n\nTavily Crawl combines both mapping and extraction operations, so the cost is the sum of both:\n\n Crawl Cost = Mapping Cost + Extraction Cost\n\nFor example:\n\n If you crawl 10 pages with basic extraction depth, you’ll be charged 1 credit for mapping (10 pages) + 2 credits for extraction (10 successful extractions ÷ 5) = 3 total credits\n If you crawl 10 pages with advanced extraction depth, you’ll be charged 1 credit for mapping + 4 credits for extraction = 5 total credits\n\n### ​ Tavily Research (beta)",

Follow these steps immediately:\n\n1. Log in to your account: Go to the Tavily Dashboard.\n2. Revoke the leaked key: Navigate to the API Keys section. Identify the compromised key and delete or revoke it immediately. This will stop any unauthorized usage.\n3. Generate a new key: Create a new API key to replace the compromised one.\n4. Update your applications: Replace the old key with the new one in your environment variables, secrets management systems, and application code. [...] To rotate your keys without downtime:\n\n1. Generate a new key: Create a new API key in the Tavily Dashboard while keeping the old one active.\n2. Update your application: Deploy your application with the new API key.\n3. Verify functionality: Ensure your application is working correctly with the new key.\n4. Revoke the old key: Once you are confirmed that the new key is in use and everything is functioning as expected, delete the old API key from the dashboard.\n\nNever hardcode API keys in your source code. Always use environment variables or a secure secrets manager to store your credentials.\n\nResearch",

In 1–3 sentences, say exactly what the field should contain and what to look for. This makes it easier for our models to interpret what you’re looking for.\n Match the structure you actually need. We use this information for benchmarking purposes, as well as to create aggregated usage reports and to understand how users are using the Platform. To the extent the EU or UK data protection laws apply, the legal basis for this processing is the [...] Opt Out of Advertising Cookies. Such information is governed by the applicable third-party index provider’s privacy policy. By sharing personal information in your query, you direct us to share the information with the applicable third-party index provider, if necessary. [## Get your API key\n\nCreate your Development or Production API keys.](https://app.tavily.com)\n\n| Environment | Requests per minute (RPM) |\n| --- | --- |\n| `Development` | 100 |\n| `Production` | 1,000 |\n\n## Crawl Endpoint Rate Limits\n\nThe crawl endpoint has a separate rate limit that applies to both development and production keys:\n\n| Environment | Requests per minute (RPM) |\n| --- | --- |\n| `Development` | 100 |\n| `Production` | 100 |\n\n1. Access to production keys requires either an active **Paid Plan** or **PAYGO** enabled. More information can be found [here](/guides/api-credits).\n2. The Tavily Search crawler does not advertise a differentiated user agent because we must avoid discrimination from websites that allow only Google to crawl them. However, if a domain or page is not crawlable by Googlebot, then Tavily Search’s bot will not crawl it either.\n\n### Indexing and Delisting\n\n* robots.txt is not used to prevent a page from being indexed. Instead, a site owner can delist a page by using the robots noindex directive.\n* Once your web page has been updated with this directive, Tavily needs to re-fetch it to apply the changes.\n\n### [​](#right-to-be-forgotten) Right to Be Forgotten\n\nIf your inquiry is about delisting web pages containing personal data about you, please follow the guidance and process of the [right to be forgotten](/documentation/Right-To-Be-Forgotten).\n\n### [​](#reporting-non-existent-pages) Reporting Non-Existent Pages\n\nIn case Tavily Search is returning a page that no longer exists, and you would like to have it delisted, you may contact us at **[[email protected]](/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#5e2d2b2e2e312c2a1e2a3f28373227703d3133)**.\n\n[Privacy Policy](/documentation/privacy)[Frequently Asked Questions](/faq/faq)",

Website Crawling & Vectorization:\n\nUse Tavily’s crawling endpoint to extract and sitemap content from a webpage URL, then embed it into a MongoDB Atlas vector index for retrieval. \n\n### [​](#2-intelligent-q&a-interface:) 2. Intelligent Q&A Interface:\n\nQuery your crawled data through a conversational agent that provides citation-backed answers while maintaining conversation history and context. The agent intelligently distinguishes between informational questions (requiring vector search) and conversational queries (using general knowledge). \n\n## [​](#try-our-crawl-to-rag-use-case) Try Our Crawl to RAG Use Case\n\n### [​](#step-1:-get-your-api-key) Step 1: Get Your API Key\n\n[## Get your Tavily API key](https://app.tavily.com)\n\n### [​](#step-2:-chat-with-tavily) Step 2: Chat with Tavily\n\n[## Launch the application](https://crawl-to-rag.tavily.com/)\n\n### [​](#step-3:-read-the-open-source-code) Step 3: Read The Open Source Code\n\n[## View Github Repository](https://github.com/tavily-ai/crawl2rag)\n\n## [​](#features) Features\n\n1. **Advanced Web Crawling**: Deep website content extraction using Tavily’s crawling API\n2. **Vector Search**: MongoDB Atlas vector search with OpenAI embeddings for semantic content retrieval\n3. **Smart Question Routing**: Automatic detection of informational vs. conversational queries\n4. **Persistent Memory**: Conversation history and context preservation using LangGraph-MongoDB checkpointing\n5. **Session Management**: Thread-based conversational persistance and vector store management\n\n[Company Research](/examples/use-cases/company-research)[Meeting Prep](/examples/use-cases/meeting-prep)",

      "raw_content": "Your search depth determines the cost of your request.\n\n Basic Search (`basic`): Each request costs 1 API credit.\n Advanced Search (`advanced`): Each request costs 2 API credits.\n\n### ​ Tavily Extract\n\nThe number of successful URL extractions and your extraction depth determines the cost of your request. You never get charged if a URL extraction fails.\n\n Basic Extract (`basic`): Every 5 successful URL extractions cost 1 API credit\n Advanced Extract (`advanced`): Every 5 successful URL extractions cost 2 API credits\n\n### ​ Tavily Map\n\nThe number of pages mapped and whether or not natural-language instructions are specified determines the cost of your request. You never get charged if a map request fails. No credit card required.\n\n## ​ Pricing Overview\n\nTavily operates on a simple, credit-based model: [...] Regular Mapping: Every 10 successful pages returned cost 1 API credit\n Map with (`instructions`): Every 10 successful pages returned cost 2 API credits\n\n### ​ Tavily Crawl\n\nTavily Crawl combines both mapping and extraction operations, so the cost is the sum of both:\n\n Crawl Cost = Mapping Cost + Extraction Cost\n\nFor example:\n\n If you crawl 10 pages with basic extraction depth, you’ll be charged 1 credit for mapping (10 pages) + 2 credits for extraction (10 successful extractions ÷ 5) = 3 total credits\n If you crawl 10 pages with advanced extraction depth, you’ll be charged 1 credit for mapping + 4 credits for extraction = 5 total credits\n\n### ​ Tavily Research (beta)",
